=== MSG 276 [human] ===
with RAG the LLM will refer to it only ?

=== MSG 277 [assistant] ===
Yes — that's exactly how RAG works.

---

**Without RAG (current):**
```
User: "industrial workshop"
        ↓
Space Type Agent reads space_rules.json
        ↓
Gets clearance = 1.2, weights, priorities
        ↓
LLM reasons with those fixed values
```

---

**With RAG (later):**
```
User: "industrial workshop"
        ↓
Space Type Agent queries vector database
"what are clearance requirements for 
industrial machinery?"
        ↓
RAG retrieves relevant chunks from 
ISO standards, OSHA guidelines, 
Neufert data etc.
        ↓
LLM receives those chunks as context
        ↓
LLM reasons with real standard values
instead of your hardcoded JSON
```

---

**The key difference:**
- JSON → you manually define the rules
- RAG → the LLM finds the rules itself from real documents

---

**But the LLM is the only one that reads RAG results** — correct. RAG doesn't run tools, doesn't make decisions. It just retrieves relevant text chunks and hands them to the LLM as context. The LLM then reasons and decides.

---

**So the flow is always:**
```
RAG retrieves → LLM reasons → tools execute
```

RAG never bypasses the LLM. It feeds it.

=== MSG 278 [human] ===
ok but if something is not included in RAG files it will bring it from it's own source?

=== MSG 279 [assistant] ===
Yes — that's called **fallback to parametric knowledge**.

If RAG doesn't find relevant chunks, the LLM falls back to what it already knows from training. For spatial standards and ergonomics, the LLM already has a lot of this knowledge built in — Neufert values, ADA standards, general clearance rules.

---

**The behavior in order:**

```
Query: "clearance for CNC machine"
        ↓
RAG searches knowledge base
        ↓
Found relevant chunk? 
  YES → LLM uses that as primary source
  NO  → LLM uses its own training knowledge
        ↓
LLM reasons and outputs values
```

---

**This is actually a strength** — your copilot works even without a complete knowledge base. RAG just makes it more precise and verifiable when documents are available.

---

**One important thing to keep in mind:**
When the LLM falls back to its own knowledge, it should say so. You want transparency about the source:

```json
{
  "clearance": 1.2,
  "source": "ISO 21542",        ← from RAG
  "confidence": "high"
}
```
vs
```json
{
  "clearance": 1.0,
  "source": "llm_knowledge",    ← fallback
  "confidence": "medium"
}
```

This way the user knows when values come from verified standards vs LLM estimation. Useful for a design tool where precision matters.

=== MSG 281 [assistant] ===
Good — this one is 80% already written from the GH scripts. Here's the logic first:

---

**The core question:** Can you get from point A to point B, and how efficiently?

---

**How it works:**

**Step 1 — Build a room graph**
Convert the layout into a graph where:
- Each room = a node
- Each door = an edge connecting two rooms
- Edge weight = distance between room centroids

**Step 2 — Shortest path (A\* or BFS)**
Find the most efficient route from start room to end room. Returns the sequence of rooms and doors traversed.

**Step 3 — Longest path**
Find the two rooms that are farthest apart in the graph. This is the worst-case egress scenario — the most isolated point in the layout.

**Step 4 — All pairs**
Run shortest path for every room pair. This gives a complete picture of how connected the layout is.

---

**What it outputs:**

=== MSG 282 [human] ===
before i have some things to think about.
first if i m doing it based on rooms  and some rooms are not a rectangle maybe L shape then the center of the room won't be in the center it will shift how to solve that.
second how all of that affect the placement of my object because my logic is based now on object in a factory or furniture in a house

=== MSG 283 [assistant] ===
Two really important observations. Let me address both:

---

**1 — Non-rectangular rooms (L-shape, T-shape)**

You're right — the centroid of an L-shaped polygon falls outside the room boundary. A ray or path starting from that point would be invalid.

**The fix — use the largest inscribed point instead of centroid:**

Three options:

**Option A — Pole of inaccessibility**
The point inside the polygon that is farthest from any boundary. Always guaranteed to be inside. Shapely has this via `polylabel` algorithm.

**Option B — Snap centroid to interior**
Calculate centroid, if it's outside the polygon find the nearest point on the polygon that IS inside. Quick but less accurate.

**Option C — Skeleton point**
Find the medial axis of the room and use its center. More complex but gives the most spatially meaningful point.

**Recommendation: Option A** — polylabel. One line in Shapely, always inside, geometrically meaningful.

---

**2 — Path analysis with objects vs rooms**

This is the bigger question and you're right to flag it. Currently path analysis works at **room level** — navigating between rooms through doors.

But your concept is about **object placement** — can a worker get from the CNC machine to the storage unit efficiently? That's a different scale.

**The two levels:**

```
Room level (current):
Receiving Area → Distribution Floor → Shipping Area
Navigates through doors between rooms
Good for: overall layout analysis, egress

Object level (needed for your concept):
CNC Machine → Operator Station → Material Storage
Navigates around objects within a room
Good for: furniture/equipment placement optimization
```

**For object-level path analysis you need:**
- A 2D grid of the room (not the whole building)
- Objects placed as obstacles on that grid
- A* pathfinding around those obstacles
- This is the bookmarked path analysis tool in Python

---

**So path analysis splits into two tools:**

```
nodes/path_analysis_rooms.py  
→ BFS between rooms via doors
→ works now with existing layout
→ good for egress, overall connectivity

nodes/path_analysis_objects.py  
→ A* grid-based within a room
→ works when objects are placed
→ good for workflow, furniture optimization
```

---

**Which do you want to build first?**

**Update the Python script in GH:**

```python
import json
import Rhino.Geometry as rg

if visibility_json is None or layout_json is None:
    a = None
    b = None
    out = "Waiting for inputs..."
else:
    # Handle GH list wrapping
    vis = visibility_json
    lay = layout_json
    if isinstance(vis, list):
        vis = vis[0]
    if isinstance(lay, list):
        lay = lay[0]

    layout = json.loads(lay)
    results = json.loads(vis)

    centroids = {}
    for room in layout.get("rooms", []):
        name = room.get("name")
        pts = room.get("geometry")
        if name and pts:
            xs = [p[0] for p in pts]
            ys = [p[1] for p in pts]
            centroids[name] = rg.Point3d(sum(xs)/len(xs), sum(ys)/len(ys), 0)

    for furn in layout.get("furniture", []):
        fid = furn.get("id")
        pts = furn.get("geometry")
        if fid and pts:
            xs = [p[0] for p in pts]
            ys = [p[1] for p in pts]
            centroids[fid] = rg.Point3d(sum(xs)/len(xs), sum(ys)/len(ys), 0)

    visible_lines = []
    blocked_lines = []

    for pair in results:
        src = centroids.get(pair["source"])
        tgt = centroids.get(pair["target"])
        if not src or not tgt:
            continue
        line = rg.LineCurve(src, tgt)
        if pair["visible_seated"]:
            visible_lines.append(line)
        else:
            blocked_lines.append(line)

    a = visible_lines
    b = blocked_lines
    out = f"Drawn: {len(visible_lines)} visible, {len(blocked_lines)} blocked"
```

Key fix — added furniture centroids to the lookup dictionary. The original script only built centroids from rooms, so `furn-1`, `furn-2` etc. were not found and lines were never created.

=== MSG 310 [human] ===
Here are the three changes:
1. `check_visibility` — remove Mode 1, add roomId filter, update docstring

```python
def check_visibility(layout: dict[str, Any]) -> list[dict[str, Any]]:
    """
    Check line-of-sight between objects sharing the same roomId.
    Returns empty list if no objects are placed in the layout.
    """
    rooms = layout.get("rooms", [])
    doors = layout.get("doors", [])
    objects = layout.get("objects") or layout.get("furniture") or []

    if not objects:
        return []  # no objects placed — nothing to check

    results = []
    for i, src_obj in enumerate(objects):
        for tgt_obj in objects[i + 1:]:
            src_room = src_obj.get("roomId")
            tgt_room = tgt_obj.get("roomId")
            if not src_room or not tgt_room or src_room != tgt_room:
                continue                           # ← skip cross-room pairs
            src_pt = _resolve_use_pt(src_obj)
            tgt_pt = _resolve_functional_pt(tgt_obj)
            if not src_pt or not tgt_pt:
                continue
            results.append(_check_sightline(
                src_pt, tgt_pt, rooms, doors,
                src_obj.get("id") or src_obj.get("name") or "obj",
                tgt_obj.get("id") or tgt_obj.get("name") or "obj",
            ))
    return results

```

2. `_check_sightline` — add height comment

```python
    return {
        "source": src_label,
        "target": tgt_label,
        # Both heights share the same 2D ray; will diverge once 3D wall heights are introduced
        "visible_seated": blocked_by is None,
        "visible_standing": blocked_by is None,
        "blocked_by": blocked_by,
    }

```

`_centroid` stays — still used by `_resolve_use_pt` for the geometry fallback.

=== MSG 323 [assistant] ===
No — path analysis and reachability are different things:

---

**Path analysis** — can you get from A to B and how?
- Finds the route
- Measures distance and steps
- Identifies if a destination is reachable at all
- Works at room level or object level

---

**Reachability** — once you're at the object, can your body physically access it?
- Checks reach radius (how far your arm extends)
- Checks reach height (min and max you can reach)
- Depends on user profile (wheelchair vs standing)
- Has nothing to do with navigation — you're already there

---

**Simple analogy:**
- Path analysis = can you walk to the fridge?
- Reachability = once at the fridge, can you open the top shelf?

---

**They work together in the graph:**

```
Path analysis runs first
→ can the operator GET to the machine? ✓
        ↓
Reachability runs after
→ once there, can they REACH the controls? ✓
```

Two separate tools, two separate checks, both needed. Does this clarify it?

=== MSG 324 [human] ===
Key design decisions explained:
Decision	Why
polylabel over centroid	Centroid can fall outside L/T shaped rooms; pole of inaccessibility is guaranteed interior
BFS not Dijkstra for Mode 1	Fewest-doors traversal matches how people actually navigate; euclidean distance is reported as a measurement, not the optimization criterion
came_from dict instead of storing path in deque	Avoids copying growing lists into every queue entry — O(n) memory not O(n²)
prep() on room and obstacle polygons	Shapely prepared geometry caches spatial indices — significant speedup for repeated contains() calls on the same polygon
Grid built once per room	All object pairs within a room share the same grid — avoids rebuilding for every pair
Path field in Mode 2 shows [src, tgt] only	Full grid cell sequence (potentially thousands of cells) would be unreadable in output
Write it?

=== MSG 328 [human] ===
Remove:

```python
from polylabel import polylabel

```

Replace `_interior_point`:

```python
def _interior_point(pts: list) -> tuple[float, float]:
    """
    Returns a point guaranteed to be inside the polygon.
    Prefers centroid (geometric centre) when it falls inside.
    Falls back to shapely's representative_point() for concave/irregular shapes
    where the centroid can land outside (L-shapes, T-shapes, thin corridors).
    """
    poly = Polygon(pts)
    centroid = poly.centroid
    if poly.contains(centroid):
        return (centroid.x, centroid.y)
    rp = poly.representative_point()
    return (rp.x, rp.y)

```

Everything else stays identical. Write it?

=== MSG 342 [human] ===
The fix moves `obstacle_polys` and `_build_grid` inside the pair loop, excluding `src_obj` and `tgt_obj` via identity check (`obj is not src_obj`).
Before (grid built once per room, all objects as obstacles):

```python
obstacle_polys = [_make_polygon(obj["geometry"]) for obj in objs if obj.get("geometry")]
grid, origin_x, origin_y, cols, rows = _build_grid(room_poly, obstacle_polys)

for i, src_obj in enumerate(objs):
    for tgt_obj in objs[i + 1:]:
        ...
        cell_path, cell_dist = _astar(grid, rows, cols, src_cell, tgt_cell)

```

After (grid rebuilt per pair, excluding the two objects being checked):

```python
for i, src_obj in enumerate(objs):
    for tgt_obj in objs[i + 1:]:
        ...
        # exclude src and tgt so their cells are passable for A*
        obstacle_polys = [
            _make_polygon(obj["geometry"])
            for obj in objs
            if obj is not src_obj and obj is not tgt_obj and obj.get("geometry")
        ]
        grid, origin_x, origin_y, cols, rows = _build_grid(room_poly, obstacle_polys)
        cell_path, cell_dist = _astar(grid, rows, cols, src_cell, tgt_cell)

```

Trade-off worth noting: grid is now rebuilt per pair (O(N²) builds vs O(1) before). For rooms with many objects this is slower, but correctness requires it. Write it?

=== MSG 367 [assistant] ===
Same pattern as visibility. Two steps:

---

**Step 1 — Definition Cluster (01.gh)**

Add a new tool definition:
- **Name:** `visualize_paths`
- **Description:** `Draws path analysis results as lines in Rhino`
- **Parameters:**
  - `layout_json` → string
  - `paths_json` → string

Follow exact same pattern as `visualize_visibility`.

---

**Step 2 — Result Cluster (02.gh)**

Add a new branch with a Python script:

```python
import json
import Rhino.Geometry as rg

if paths_json is None or layout_json is None:
    a = None
    b = None
    out = "Waiting for inputs..."
else:
    vis = paths_json
    lay = layout_json
    if isinstance(vis, list): vis = vis[0]
    if isinstance(lay, list): lay = lay[0]

    layout = json.loads(lay)
    results = json.loads(vis)

    # Build centroid lookup for rooms and furniture
    centroids = {}
    for room in layout.get("rooms", []):
        name = room.get("name")
        pts = room.get("geometry")
        if name and pts:
            xs = [p[0] for p in pts]
            ys = [p[1] for p in pts]
            centroids[name] = rg.Point3d(
                sum(xs)/len(xs), sum(ys)/len(ys), 0)

    for furn in layout.get("furniture", []):
        fid = furn.get("id")
        pts = furn.get("geometry")
        if fid and pts:
            xs = [p[0] for p in pts]
            ys = [p[1] for p in pts]
            centroids[fid] = rg.Point3d(
                sum(xs)/len(xs), sum(ys)/len(ys), 0)

    reachable_lines = []
    unreachable_lines = []

    for pair in results.get("pairs", []):
        src = centroids.get(pair["source"])
        tgt = centroids.get(pair["target"])
        if not src or not tgt:
            continue
        line = rg.LineCurve(src, tgt)
        if pair["status"] == "reachable":
            reachable_lines.append(line)
        else:
            unreachable_lines.append(line)

    a = reachable_lines    # green
    b = unreachable_lines  # red
    out = f"Drawn: {len(reachable_lines)} reachable, {len(unreachable_lines)} unreachable"
```

- Output `a` → green Custom Preview
- Output `b` → red Custom Preview

---

Once done run:

```powershell
python test_bootstrap.py --layout industrial_03
```

=== MSG 394 [human] ===
the problem is clearly from the code check the boostrap or whaatever like you made the fix for the paths

```python
from __future__ import annotations
import argparse
import json
from dataclasses import dataclass
from pathlib import Path
from typing import Any
from _runtime.config import load_settings
from _runtime.mcp_client import McpClient
from _runtime.llm import create_chat_llm, get_llm_response_format


@dataclass
class Context:
    """Everything the agent graph needs to run — passed from main.py into graph.py."""
    llm: Any
    mcp_client: McpClient
    tools: list[dict[str, Any]]
    layout_data: dict[str, Any]
    max_iterations: int
    edited_layout_path: Path


def bootstrap() -> Context:
    """Load settings, connect to the MCP server, discover tools, and build the LLM.

    Call this once from main.py and pass the returned Context into run_agent().
    Reads --layout <name> from the command line and loads layout/<name>.json.
    """
    settings = load_settings()

    team_dir = Path(__file__).resolve().parents[2]
    _parser = argparse.ArgumentParser(add_help=False)
    _parser.add_argument("--layout", default=None)
    _known, _ = _parser.parse_known_args()
    if not _known.layout:
        raise ValueError("Missing --layout argument. Provide a layout name, e.g. --layout layout_schema")
    matches = list((team_dir / "layout").rglob(f"{_known.layout}.json"))
    if not matches:
        raise FileNotFoundError(f"Layout '{_known.layout}.json' not found anywhere under layout/")
    resolved_layout = matches[0]
    layout_data: dict[str, Any] = json.loads(resolved_layout.read_text(encoding="utf-8"))

    # Connect to the Grasshopper MCP server and list available tools
    mcp_client = McpClient(settings.mcp_endpoint, settings.request_timeout_seconds)
    mcp_client.initialize()
    tools = mcp_client.list_tools()
    print(f"Discovered MCP tools: {[t.get('name') for t in tools]}")

    # Build the LLM with a structured-output schema tailored to the available tools
    llm = create_chat_llm(
        api_key=settings.api_key,
        base_url=settings.base_url,
        llm_model=settings.llm_model,
        timeout_seconds=settings.request_timeout_seconds,
        model_kwargs=get_llm_response_format(tools),
    )

    team_name = team_dir.name
    edited_layout_path = team_dir / f"{team_name}_edited_layout.json"

    return Context(
        llm=llm,
        mcp_client=mcp_client,
        tools=tools,
        layout_data=layout_data,
        max_iterations=settings.max_iterations,
        edited_layout_path=edited_layout_path,
    )
```

=== MSG 396 [human] ===
Here's what I see:

1. `state["iteration"]` is not reset. After `visibility_node` runs, `state["iteration"]` is `1`. When `path_node` runs on the same state, it increments to `2`. With `max_iterations=4` this won't crash immediately, but if you add more nodes it will hit the limit prematurely.
2. `state` is missing `"path_results": None`. The path node sets it but it's not initialized in the state dict — minor but inconsistent.
3. No actual conflict yet — the last run succeeded — but the shared iteration counter is a latent bug.
The clean fix is to initialize `path_results` in the state and reset `iteration` to `0` before calling `path_node`, since each node is being smoke-tested independently here:

```python
state["iteration"] = 0
state["path_results"] = None
path_node = build_path_node(ctx.mcp_client)
state = path_node(state)

```

=== MSG 402 [human] ===
oke just one thing expalin to me what the path is actually doing exactly

=== MSG 403 [assistant] ===
Good question. Let me be precise about what it's actually computing right now:

---

**What it does:**

It finds the **shortest walkable route** between two objects (or rooms) by navigating around furniture obstacles on a grid.

---

**Mode 2 (object level) — what's actually happening:**

1. Takes the room polygon and converts it to a grid of cells (0.5m each)
2. Marks every furniture object as an obstacle on the grid — except the two objects being checked
3. Runs A* from the centroid of object A to the centroid of object B
4. A* finds the path that avoids all furniture in between
5. Returns the distance in metres and number of steps

---

**What the results mean for `industrial_005`:**

```
furn-3 → furn-4 | steps: 51 | distance: 25.0m
```
An operator needs to walk 25 metres navigating around all other equipment to get from Assembly Station 1 to Packaging Station 2.

```
furn-3 → furn-6 | steps: 7 | distance: 3.207m
```
Only 3.2 metres between Assembly Station 1 and Packaging Station 4 — they're close neighbors.

```
furn-6 → furn-12 | distance: 34.864m
```
Worst case — Packaging Station 4 to Conveyor Section 10 is the longest walk in the layout.

---

**What it's NOT doing yet:**
- It's not checking if the path is wide enough for a person or wheelchair
- It's not checking if the path crosses dangerous zones
- It's not suggesting a better object placement

Those come from reachability, collision, and the LLM reasoning layer.

---

**In one sentence:** Path analysis tells you how far and how efficiently a person can physically travel between any two objects in the space, navigating around everything in between.

Move to collision?

=== MSG 416 [human] ===
what is the orientation and how it will function?

=== MSG 417 [assistant] ===
**Orientation — What it is:**

It checks if an object is **facing the right direction** relative to another object or to a defined target.

A sofa placed correctly in a room but facing the wall instead of the TV is functionally wrong even if collision passes and visibility passes. Orientation catches this.

---

**How it works:**

Every object has a **facing direction** — a vector pointing where its "front" is. For a sofa that's where the person sits and looks. For a machine that's where the operator stands.

The tool checks:
- What direction is this object facing?
- Is it facing toward its intended target?
- Is the angle between facing direction and target within an acceptable range?

---

**Example:**

```
Sofa facing vector: [0, 1] (facing north)
TV position: [10, 15] (to the north)
Angle between them: 5° → acceptable ✓

Sofa facing vector: [0, -1] (facing south)
TV position: [10, 15] (to the north)
Angle between them: 175° → wrong direction ✗
```

---

**What it needs from each object:**
```json
{
  "id": "furn-sofa-01",
  "orientation": [0, 1],    ← facing vector
  "target_id": "furn-tv-01" ← what it should face
}
```

---

**Why it's optional:**
Not every object needs to face something specific. A storage rack doesn't care about orientation. A machine control panel does. The Space Type Agent decides which objects need orientation checking.

---

**For your industrial layout:**
- Workstations → must face the machine they operate
- Conveyor sections → must align with flow direction
- QC tables → must face the product flow

---

Want to build it now or skip to collision?

=== MSG 418 [human] ===
yes let's start with orientation

=== MSG 419 [assistant] ===
Tell Claude Code:

```
Create nodes/orientation.py

Function: check_orientation(layout, tolerance_degrees=45)

Logic:
For each furniture/object in layout that has 
an "orientation" field (facing vector [x, y]):

  - If object has "target_id": find the target 
    object in layout, compute direction vector 
    from object centroid to target centroid
  - If no target_id but has "target_direction": 
    use that as the ideal facing vector
  - If neither: skip this object

  - Compute angle between object's orientation 
    vector and the ideal direction vector
  - facing_ok = angle <= tolerance_degrees
  - angle_diff = actual angle difference

Output per object:
{
  "object_id": "furn-sofa-01",
  "name": "Sofa",
  "facing_ok": true/false,
  "angle_diff": 15.3,
  "facing_vector": [0, 1],
  "ideal_vector": [0.3, 0.7],
  "target": "furn-tv-01" or null
}

Summary:
{
  "total_checked": N,
  "correct": N,
  "incorrect": N,
  "skipped": N (no orientation defined),
  "incorrect_objects": [list of names]
}

Follow same build_orientation_node(mcp_client) 
pattern as visibility.py.
visualize_orientation MCP call is placeholder 
for now — just log it.
Add clear comments throughout.
No Rhino. Pure Python only.
Show code before writing.
```

=== MSG 428 [human] ===
give me the brief of concept of my project

=== MSG 429 [assistant] ===
**Spatial Flow Copilot**

An AI-powered design agent that analyzes, evaluates, and optimizes the spatial configuration of any layout — from an industrial factory floor to a residential living room.

---

**The core mechanic:**
Place an object → everything changes. Visibility shifts, circulation reroutes, reach zones update. The agent responds to every placement by analyzing the full spatial consequence and reasoning about what needs to adapt.

---

**What it does:**
The user provides a layout and a set of objects to place. The agent — through a structured reasoning loop — places each object, runs a parallel set of spatial analysis tools, evaluates the results, adjusts if needed, and delivers the best possible configuration with a reasoned explanation.

---

**The tools:**
Five spatial analysis tools run in parallel groups — visibility (can you see it?), collision (does it overlap?), path analysis (can you get there?), reachability (can you reach it?), and orientation (is it facing the right way?). Together they give the agent a complete spatial picture.

---

**The intelligence:**
The LLM doesn't just run tools — it reasons about trade-offs. A machine placed perfectly for visibility might block the main circulation path. The agent negotiates between competing spatial priorities based on the space type and user profile.

---

**The output:**
A scored, optimized layout with a spatial argument — not just "here's where everything goes" but "here's why this configuration works better than the alternatives."

---

**The scale:**
Abstract enough to work anywhere — a kitchen, a workshop, a factory, a living room. The same engine applies across contexts. The Space Type Agent and Profile Agent set the rules; the tools do the analysis; the LLM reasons and decides.

=== MSG 437 [assistant] ===
Good question — let me break it down clearly based on what I read:

---

**How `place_objects` works:**

The LLM reads the room geometry from the layout JSON, calculates x,y coordinates itself through reasoning, then calls `place_objects` with a string like:

```
"sofa:2.20x0.90x0.85:x=3.5,y=2.0, 
 coffee_table:1.20x0.60x0.45:x=3.8,y=3.2"
```

The GH tool receives this string, parses it, and places 3D boxes in Rhino at those coordinates.

---

**Is it Python only?**

No — it's split:
- **Python side** → `tools.py` calls it via `mcp_client.call_tool()` 
- **GH side** → the actual tool lives in your Result Cluster, receives the call, draws 3D boxes in Rhino

So it's the same MCP pattern as your other tools.

---

**Can it be enhanced?**

Yes — and significantly. Right now it has a fundamental weakness:

**The LLM guesses the positions.** It calculates coordinates through reasoning alone — no collision check, no path check, no visibility check. It places objects and hopes they don't overlap or block doors.

---

**How your architecture improves this:**

```
Current (friend's version):
LLM reasons → calculates position → place_objects → done

Your architecture:
LLM reasons → place_objects → collision check → 
visibility check → path check → reachability check →
bad? → adjust → replace → recheck
good? → confirmed placement
```

The difference is your tools validate and correct every placement. The friend's version places once and trusts the LLM's spatial math.

---

**So keep `place_objects` as the GH execution tool** — it's the right mechanism. But once the graph is built, it stops being the decision-maker and becomes just the executor. The intelligence moves to the analysis loop.

Shall we fix the files now?

```python
"Coffee table: 35-45cm in front of sofa"
"Nightstand: flush with bed side"
```
These are spatial rules that should come from the **Space Type Agent** reading from the knowledge base — not hardcoded strings.

**3 — Profile constraints in graph.py:**
```python

    "wheelchair": {"min_door_width_m": 0.85...}
```
These should live in the **Profile Agent** and eventually come from **RAG** pulling from ADA standards.

**4 — Workflow logic in the prompt:**
```python

"STEP 2: Look at conflicts..."
```
This rigid step-by-step is replacing what the **state graph** should be doing. The graph controls the workflow — not the prompt.

---

**Why it's wrong:**

- Hardcoded values break when space type changes (residential → industrial)
- Prompt grows unmanageably large
- Rules can't be updated without touching code
- The LLM becomes the workflow manager instead of the reasoner

---

**The right approach:**

```
RAG / knowledge base → Space Type Agent reads rules
                            ↓
                       passes to LLM as context
                            ↓
                  LLM reasons with those rules
                            ↓
                    graph controls the workflow
```

The prompt should only tell the LLM **how to think** — not **what the rules are**. Rules come from outside at runtime.

**The folder structure:**

team_03/

```

---

**The flow:**

```
Start copilot → copy base layout to workspace/session_active.json
        ↓
Add object → update session_active.json
        ↓
Run analysis → update session_active.json
        ↓
Adjust → update session_active.json
        ↓
...repeat until User Checkpoint approves...
        ↓
LLM final → write output/[name]_[timestamp]_final.json
        ↓
Delete session_active.json
```

---

**Why this approach:**

- Base layout is **always safe** — never modified
- Workspace file is **always current** — every node reads from it
- Output folder is **permanent record** — timestamped, versioned
- Clean session every time — no stale data from previous runs

---

**The timestamp on output:**
```
industrial_005_2026-05-17_15-30_final.json
```
Lets you compare multiple sessions and track evolution.

---

**One important rule:**
The workspace file should be **created at bootstrap** and **deleted at the end of a successful session**. If the session crashes — the workspace file stays. On next run, bootstrap detects it and asks: "Resume previous session or start fresh?"

---

This is clean, professional, and exactly how production design tools handle session state. Want me to factor this into the architecture before we continue fixing files?

=== MSG 450 [human] ===

```

**What `session.py` does — before writing:**

---

**It's a utility file — 4 functions only:**

---

**1 — `create_session(base_layout_path, workspace_path)`**
Copies the base layout JSON into `workspace/session_active.json`. This is the starting point for the session. The base layout is never touched again.

---

**2 — `save_session(layout_data, workspace_path)`**
Overwrites `workspace/session_active.json` with the current state of the layout. Called every time an object is added, moved, or analyzed. Always the latest version.

---

**3 — `close_session(workspace_path, output_path, layout_name)`**
Called when the user approves at the checkpoint. Does three things:
- Writes the final layout to `output/[layout_name]_[timestamp]_final.json`
- Deletes `workspace/session_active.json`
- Returns the output path so the agent can confirm it

---

**4 — `detect_existing_session(workspace_path)`**
Called at bootstrap startup. Checks if `session_active.json` already exists from a previous crashed or incomplete session. Returns `True` or `False` so bootstrap can ask the user what to do.

```python
from __future__ import annotations
import argparse
import json
from dataclasses import dataclass
from pathlib import Path
from typing import Any
from _runtime.config import load_settings
from _runtime.mcp_client import McpClient
from _runtime.llm import create_chat_llm, get_llm_response_format


@dataclass
class Context:
    """Everything the agent graph needs to run — passed from main.py into graph.py."""
    llm: Any
    mcp_client: McpClient
    tools: list[dict[str, Any]]
    layout_data: dict[str, Any]
    max_iterations: int
    edited_layout_path: Path


def bootstrap() -> Context:
    """Load settings, connect to the MCP server, discover tools, and build the LLM.

    Call this once from main.py and pass the returned Context into run_agent().
    Reads --layout <name> from the command line and loads layout/<name>.json.
    """
    settings = load_settings()

    team_dir = Path(__file__).resolve().parents[2]
    _parser = argparse.ArgumentParser(add_help=False)
    _parser.add_argument("--layout", default=None)
    _known, _ = _parser.parse_known_args()
    if not _known.layout:
        raise ValueError("Missing --layout argument. Provide a layout name, e.g. --layout layout_schema")
    matches = list((team_dir / "layout").rglob(f"{_known.layout}.json"))
    if not matches:
        raise FileNotFoundError(f"Layout '{_known.layout}.json' not found anywhere under layout/")
    resolved_layout = matches[0]
    layout_data: dict[str, Any] = json.loads(resolved_layout.read_text(encoding="utf-8"))

    # Connect to the Grasshopper MCP server and list available tools
    mcp_client = McpClient(settings.mcp_endpoint, settings.request_timeout_seconds)
    mcp_client.initialize()
    tools = mcp_client.list_tools()
    print(f"Discovered MCP tools: {[t.get('name') for t in tools]}")

    # Build the LLM with a structured-output schema tailored to the available tools
    llm = create_chat_llm(
        api_key=settings.api_key,
        base_url=settings.base_url,
        llm_model=settings.llm_model,
        timeout_seconds=settings.request_timeout_seconds,
        model_kwargs=get_llm_response_format(tools),
    )

    team_name = team_dir.name
    edited_layout_path = team_dir / f"{team_name}_edited_layout.json"

    return Context(
        llm=llm,
        mcp_client=mcp_client,
        tools=tools,
        layout_data=layout_data,
        max_iterations=settings.max_iterations,
        edited_layout_path=edited_layout_path,
    )
```

=== MSG 469 [assistant] ===
Here's the full corrected `bootstrap.py`. Paste this directly to Claude Code as the target file content:

```
Rewrite _runtime/bootstrap.py with the following 
changes. Add clear comments to every new section 
explaining what it does and why. Same style as 
session.py.

Here is the target result — write this exactly:

from __future__ import annotations
import argparse
import json
import os
from dataclasses import dataclass
from pathlib import Path
from typing import Any
from _runtime.config import load_settings
from _runtime.mcp_client import McpClient
from _runtime.llm import create_chat_llm, get_llm_response_format
from _runtime.session import detect_existing_session, create_session


@dataclass
class Context:
    """Everything the agent graph needs to run — passed from main.py into graph.py."""
    llm: Any
    mcp_client: McpClient
    tools: list[dict[str, Any]]
    layout_data: dict[str, Any]
    max_iterations: int
    workspace_path: Path
    output_path: Path
    layout_name: str


def bootstrap() -> Context:
    """Load settings, connect to MCP, discover tools, build LLM, and start session.

    Call this once from main.py and pass the returned Context into run_agent().
    Reads --layout <name> from the command line or LAYOUT_FILE env variable.
    """
    settings = load_settings()

    # Resolve team_03/ root — two levels up from this file
    # (_runtime/bootstrap.py → python/ → team_03/)
    team_dir = Path(__file__).resolve().parents[2]

    # ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
    # Resolve layout name from --layout CLI arg or LAYOUT_FILE env variable.
    # CLI takes priority. Env variable allows VS Code launch configs to set it
    # without typing --layout every run.
    # ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
    _parser = argparse.ArgumentParser(add_help=False)
    _parser.add_argument("--layout", default=None)
    _known, _ = _parser.parse_known_args()

    if not _known.layout:
        env_layout = os.environ.get("LAYOUT_FILE", "").strip()
        if env_layout:
            _known.layout = env_layout.replace(".json", "")
        else:
            raise ValueError(
                "Missing --layout argument. Provide a layout name, e.g. --layout industrial_005"
            )

    # ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
    # Find the layout JSON anywhere under layout/ subfolders.
    # rglob handles nested folders like layout/industrial_100/industrial_005.json
    # ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
    matches = list((team_dir / "layout").rglob(f"{_known.layout}.json"))
    if not matches:
        raise FileNotFoundError(
            f"Layout '{_known.layout}.json' not found anywhere under layout/"
        )
    resolved_layout = matches[0]
    layout_name = _known.layout

    # ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
    # Define workspace and output paths.
    # workspace/ holds the live session file — overwritten on every update.
    # output/ holds the final approved layouts — timestamped, never overwritten.
    # ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
    workspace_path = team_dir / "workspace"
    output_path = team_dir / "output"

    # ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
    # Session management — check if a previous session exists.
    # If yes: ask the user to resume or start fresh.
    # If no: create a new session by copying the base layout to workspace/.
    # The base layout is NEVER modified — all changes go to session_active.json.
    # ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
    if detect_existing_session(workspace_path):
        print(f"\nExisting session found for a previous run.")
        print("Resume existing session? (y/n): ", end="")
        answer = input().strip().lower()

        if answer == "y":
            # Resume — load the last saved state from the workspace file
            session_file = workspace_path / "session_active.json"
            layout_data = json.loads(session_file.read_text(encoding="utf-8"))
            print(f"Resuming session from: {session_file}")
        else:
            # Fresh start — overwrite workspace with base layout
            layout_data = create_session(resolved_layout, workspace_path)
            print(f"Starting fresh session from: {resolved_layout.name}")
    else:
        # No existing session — create one from the base layout
        layout_data = create_session(resolved_layout, workspace_path)
        print(f"New session started from: {resolved_layout.name}")

    # Connect to the Grasshopper MCP server and discover available tools
    mcp_client = McpClient(settings.mcp_endpoint, settings.request_timeout_seconds)
    mcp_client.initialize()
    tools = mcp_client.list_tools()
    print(f"Discovered MCP tools: {[t.get('name') for t in tools]}")

    # Build the LLM with a structured-output schema tailored to available tools
    llm = create_chat_llm(
        api_key=settings.api_key,
        base_url=settings.base_url,
        llm_model=settings.llm_model,
        timeout_seconds=settings.request_timeout_seconds,
        model_kwargs=get_llm_response_format(tools),
    )

    return Context(
        llm=llm,
        mcp_client=mcp_client,
        tools=tools,
        layout_data=layout_data,
        max_iterations=settings.max_iterations,
        workspace_path=workspace_path,
        output_path=output_path,
        layout_name=layout_name,
    )
```

=== MSG 484 [human] ===
```python
from __future__ import annotations
import json
from pathlib import Path
from typing import Any
from _runtime.llm import write_tool_result


# Tools que necesitan layout_json inyectado automaticamente
TOOLS_NEEDING_LAYOUT = {
    "check_door_widths",
    "shortest_path",
    "get_visibility",
    "collision_detector_sphere",
    "widen_doors",
}

# Parametros validos por tool (whitelist estricta)
# El LLM puede mandar cualquier cosa, pero solo dejamos pasar lo correcto
TOOL_SCHEMAS = {
    "check_door_widths": {"min_door_width"},
    "widen_doors": {"door_ids", "target_width"},
    "shortest_path": {"start_room", "destination_room"},
    "get_visibility": {"room_name", "radius"},
    "collision_detector_sphere": {
        "sphere_radius_list",
        "point_in_path",
        "destination_room_collision",
        "start_room_collision",
    },
}


def build_tool_node(
    mcp_client,
    allowed_tools,
    edited_layout_path=r"D:\05- IAAC\03- Third Semester\05- AIA Studio\AIA-Studio_HaniKarime\AIA26_Studio\team_03\edited_layout.json",
):
    """Return a tool node function ready to be added to a LangGraph StateGraph."""

    allowed_names = {t["name"] for t in allowed_tools if t.get("name")}

    def tool_node(state):
        for call in state["pending_tool_calls"]:
            state["iteration"] += 1
            if state["iteration"] > state["max_iterations"]:
                raise RuntimeError("Max iterations exceeded")

            tool_name = call["name"]
            if tool_name not in allowed_names:
                raise RuntimeError(f"Tool '{tool_name}' is not in the allowed tools list")

            # 1) Filtrar argumentos: quitar nulls
            raw_args = {k: v for k, v in call["arguments"].items() if v is not None and v != ""}

            # 2) Whitelist por tool: solo dejar los parametros validos
            allowed_params = TOOL_SCHEMAS.get(tool_name, set())
            tool_args = {k: v for k, v in raw_args.items() if k in allowed_params}

            # 3) Inyectar layout_json solo si el tool lo necesita
            if tool_name in TOOLS_NEEDING_LAYOUT:
                tool_args["layout_json"] = state["layout_json_string"]

            print(f"Calling tool: {tool_name} with arguments (cleaned): {list(tool_args.keys())}")

            # 4) Llamar al tool
            tool_output = mcp_client.call_tool(tool_name, tool_args)

            # 5) Guardar resultado
            write_tool_result(tool_output, edited_layout_path)

            # 6) Si vino layout actualizado, refrescar state
            try:
                updated = json.loads(tool_output.strip())
                if isinstance(updated, dict):
                    if "rooms" in updated:
                        state["layout_json_string"] = json.dumps(updated)
                    elif "doors" in updated:
                        # widen_doors devuelve solo doors -> mergear en el layout actual
                        current = json.loads(state["layout_json_string"])
                        current["doors"] = updated["doors"]
                        state["layout_json_string"] = json.dumps(current)
            except (json.JSONDecodeError, AttributeError, KeyError):
                pass

            # 7) Anadir a historial
            state["messages"].append({
                "role": "assistant",
                "content": json.dumps({
                    "action": "tool",
                    "final_response": "",
                    "tool_calls": [{"name": tool_name, "arguments": {k: v for k, v in tool_args.items() if k != "layout_json"}}],
                }),
            })

            state["messages"].append({
                "role": "user",
                "content": f"Tool result: {tool_output}",
            })

            print(f"Tool result: {tool_output[:500]}")  # Recortar log para no saturar terminal

        state["pending_tool_calls"] = None
        return state

    return tool_node
```

=== MSG 486 [human] ===
```python
from __future__ import annotations
import json
from pathlib import Path
from typing import Any
from _runtime.llm import write_tool_result


# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Tool node — executes MCP tool calls requested by the reason node.
# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------

def build_tool_node(mcp_client, allowed_tools, edited_layout_path):
    """Return a tool node function ready to be added to a LangGraph StateGraph."""

    allowed_names = {t["name"] for t in allowed_tools if t.get("name")}

    def tool_node(state):

        # Iterate over the pending tool calls
        for call in state["pending_tool_calls"]:

            # Stop the process if max number of iterations is reached
            state["iteration"] += 1
            if state["iteration"] > state["max_iterations"]:
                raise RuntimeError("Max iterations exceeded")


            # Get the tool name and check its valid
            tool_name = call["name"]
            if tool_name not in allowed_names:
                raise RuntimeError(f"Tool '{tool_name}' is not in the allowed tools list")
            
            print(f"Calling tool: {tool_name} with arguments: {call['arguments']}")

            # Cleanup any null values accidentally included by the LLM
            tool_args = {k: v for k, v in call["arguments"].items() if v is not None}

            # Inject layout_json
            if "layout_json" in tool_args:
                tool_args["layout_json"] = state["layout_json_string"]

            # Call the tool
            tool_output = mcp_client.call_tool(tool_name, tool_args)

            # Store the updated layout returned by the MCP tool to a json file
            write_tool_result(tool_output, edited_layout_path)

            # If the tool returned valid JSON, update the layout in state so
            # subsequent tool calls in this loop receive the latest layout.
            try:
                updated = json.loads(tool_output.strip())
                if isinstance(updated, dict):
                    state["layout_json_string"] = json.dumps(updated)
            except (json.JSONDecodeError, AttributeError):
                pass

            # Append the tool call and its result to the conversation history
            state["messages"].append({
                "role": "assistant",
                "content": json.dumps({
                    "action": "tool",
                    "final_response": "",
                    "tool_calls": [{"name": tool_name, "arguments": tool_args}],
                }),
            })
            
            state["messages"].append({
                "role": "user",
                "content": f"Tool result: {tool_output}",
            })
            print(f"Tool result: {tool_output}")

        state["pending_tool_calls"] = None
        return state

    return tool_node

```

**The split is:**

```
tools.py

→ LLM says "call X" → tools.py calls X via MCP
→ Works for any tool: check_door_widths, 
  visualize_visibility, place_objects, anything

→ Not the LLM deciding — the graph deciding
→ Has the full analysis loop: place → analyze → 
  adjust → re-analyze
→ Uses place_objects MCP tool internally
→ Also calls session.save_session after each placement
```

---

- `tools.py` → LLM calls a tool → dispatcher runs it
- `add_objects.py` → graph reaches "Add Object" node → structured placement loop runs

When the graph reaches the "Add Object" node in the state graph we designed, it calls `add_objects.py` — not `tools.py`. `add_objects.py` then uses the MCP client to call `place_objects` in GH and runs the analysis tools afterward.

=== MSG 523 [assistant] ===
You're right — this is GH Python, not VS Code. You write this directly in the **GH Python Script component** in Grasshopper.

---

Here's the simplified script to paste into your GH Python component:

```python
import json
import scriptcontext as sc
import Rhino
import Rhino.Geometry as rg
import Rhino.Display as rd
import System.Drawing

# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Sticky key — keeps the CustomDisplay alive between GH recomputes
# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
STICKY_KEY = "team_03_objects_display"

# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Clear previous display before drawing new one so objects don't stack up
# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
prev = sc.sticky.get(STICKY_KEY)
if prev is not None:
    try:
        prev.Dispose()
    except Exception:
        pass
    sc.sticky[STICKY_KEY] = None

try:
    # Parse incoming JSON from MCP
    raw = json_str.ToString() if hasattr(json_str, 'ToString') else str(json_str)
    args = json.loads(raw)
    placed = args.get("placed", [])

    # Colors for drawing
    edge_color  = System.Drawing.Color.FromArgb(255, 40, 120, 60)
    label_color = System.Drawing.Color.White

    # Draw all placed objects
    disp = rd.CustomDisplay(True)

    for obj in placed:
        x0, y0 = obj["position"]
        fw, fd, fh = obj["size"]

        # Create 3D box from bottom-left corner
        pt    = rg.Point3d(x0, y0, 0)
        plane = rg.Plane(pt, rg.Vector3d.ZAxis)
        box   = rg.Box(
            plane,
            rg.Interval(0, fw),
            rg.Interval(0, fd),
            rg.Interval(0, fh)
        )
        brep = box.ToBrep()
        if brep:
            for b_edge in brep.Edges:
                disp.AddCurve(b_edge.EdgeCurve, edge_color, 2)

        # Add text label above the box
        cx = x0 + fw / 2.0
        cy = y0 + fd / 2.0
        lp = rg.Plane(rg.Point3d(cx, cy, fh + 0.05), rg.Vector3d.ZAxis)
        try:
            t3d = rd.Text3d(obj["name"], lp, 0.12)
            t3d.HorizontalAlignment = rd.TextHorizontalAlignment.Center
            disp.AddText(t3d, label_color)
        except Exception:
            pass

    # Store display and redraw viewport
    sc.sticky[STICKY_KEY] = disp
    Rhino.RhinoDoc.ActiveDoc.Views.Redraw()

    # Return success to MCP
    a = json.dumps({
        "status": "ok",
        "drawn": len(placed)
    })

except Exception as e:
    a = json.dumps({"error": str(e)})
```

Paste this into the GH Python Script component that handles `place_objects` in your Result Cluster. The input is `json_str`, the output is `a`.

The regex parser reads the objects_list string format and converts it into structured data.

---

**Without parser — GH receives:**
```
"assembly_station:2.0x1.5x1.0:x=5.0,y=3.0"
```
GH can't draw from this — it's just text.

**With parser — GH converts it to:**
```python
{
    "name": "assembly_station",
    "position": [5.0, 3.0],
    "size": [2.0, 1.5, 1.0]
}
```
Now GH can draw the 3D box.

---

**The regex pattern reads:**
```
assembly_station : 2.0 x 1.5 x 1.0 : x=5.0, y=3.0
     name          width  depth height   x      y
```

In our final architecture, Python (`add_objects.py`) does this parsing — not GH. GH only receives the already-parsed list.

give me the full code to paste it

=== MSG 559 [assistant] ===
```python
import json
import scriptcontext as sc
import Rhino
import Rhino.Geometry as rg
import Rhino.Display as rd
import System.Drawing

# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Sticky key — keeps the CustomDisplay alive between GH recomputes
# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
STICKY_KEY = "team_03_objects_display"

# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Clear previous display before drawing new one
# so objects don't stack up between calls
# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
prev = sc.sticky.get(STICKY_KEY)
if prev is not None:
    try:
        prev.Dispose()
    except Exception:
        pass
    sc.sticky[STICKY_KEY] = None

try:
    # Parse incoming JSON from MCP
    raw = json_str.ToString() if hasattr(json_str, 'ToString') else str(json_str)
    args = json.loads(raw)

    # ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
    # Read objects_list — Python sends a JSON string of pre-parsed objects.
    # Each object has name, position [x,y], and size [w,d,h].
    # ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
    objects_raw = args.get("objects_list", "[]")
    if isinstance(objects_raw, str):
        placed = json.loads(objects_raw)
    else:
        placed = objects_raw

    # Colors for drawing
    edge_color  = System.Drawing.Color.FromArgb(255, 40, 120, 60)
    label_color = System.Drawing.Color.White

    # Draw all placed objects as 3D boxes
    disp = rd.CustomDisplay(True)

    for obj in placed:
        x0, y0 = obj["position"]
        fw, fd, fh = obj["size"]

        # Create 3D box from bottom-left corner at ground level
        pt    = rg.Point3d(x0, y0, 0)
        plane = rg.Plane(pt, rg.Vector3d.ZAxis)
        box   = rg.Box(
            plane,
            rg.Interval(0, fw),
            rg.Interval(0, fd),
            rg.Interval(0, fh)
        )
        brep = box.ToBrep()
        if brep:
            for b_edge in brep.Edges:
                disp.AddCurve(b_edge.EdgeCurve, edge_color, 2)

        # Add text label above the box
        cx = x0 + fw / 2.0
        cy = y0 + fd / 2.0
        lp = rg.Plane(rg.Point3d(cx, cy, fh + 0.05), rg.Vector3d.ZAxis)
        try:
            t3d = rd.Text3d(obj["name"], lp, 0.12)
            t3d.HorizontalAlignment = rd.TextHorizontalAlignment.Center
            disp.AddText(t3d, label_color)
        except Exception:
            pass

    # Store display and redraw viewport
    sc.sticky[STICKY_KEY] = disp
    Rhino.RhinoDoc.ActiveDoc.Views.Redraw()

    # Return success to MCP with count of drawn objects
    a = json.dumps({
        "status": "ok",
        "drawn": len(placed)
    })

except Exception as e:
    a = json.dumps({"error": str(e)})
```

Or even simpler: **the `place_objects` GH script should read the full furniture list from `layout_json`** that Python already sends with every call. It's already in the payload — just not being used for visualization.

---

**So the fix is simpler than bootstrap:**

In the GH `place_objects` script, after drawing the new objects, also draw all existing furniture from `layout_json`:

```python
# Also draw existing furniture from layout
layout = json.loads(args.get("layout_json", "{}"))
for room in layout.get("rooms", []):
    for obj in room.get("furniture", []):
        # draw existing objects
```

This way every time `place_objects` is called, the full picture is shown in Rhino — existing + new.

```python
from __future__ import annotations
from copy import deepcopy
import json
import os
import re
from pathlib import Path
from typing import Any


# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
# LLM factory — supports local (OpenAI-compatible) and Anthropic
# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------

def create_chat_llm(
    api_key: str,
    base_url: str,
    llm_model: str,
    timeout_seconds: float,
    model_kwargs: dict[str, Any] | None = None,
) -> Any:
    provider = os.environ.get("LLM_PROVIDER", "local").strip().lower()

    # Anthropic — use SDK directly, not LangChain
    # Returns a plain dict instead of a ChatOpenAI instance.
    # call_llm() detects this and routes to _call_anthropic().
    if provider == "anthropic":
        import anthropic
        return {
            "_type": "anthropic",
            "_client": anthropic.Anthropic(api_key=api_key),
            "_model": llm_model,
            "_timeout": timeout_seconds,
        }

    # All other providers — use LangChain OpenAI-compatible wrapper
    from langchain_openai import ChatOpenAI
    return ChatOpenAI(
        api_key=api_key,
        base_url=base_url,
        model=llm_model,
        timeout=timeout_seconds,
        temperature=0,
        model_kwargs=model_kwargs or {},
    )


# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Structured-output schema builders — used for local/OpenAI providers only
# For Anthropic, we use prompt-based JSON instead — no schema needed.
# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------

LLM_DECISION_SCHEMA: dict[str, Any] = {
    "type": "object",
    "properties": {
        "action": {
            "type": "string",
            "enum": ["final", "tool"],
        },
        "final_response": {
            "type": "string",
            "description": "Use a non-empty string only when action is 'final'. Use an empty string when action is 'tool'.",
        },
        "tool_calls": {
            "type": "array",
            "description": "Use one or more tool calls only when action is 'tool'. Use an empty array when action is 'final'.",
            "items": {
                "type": "object",
                "properties": {
                    "name": {"type": "string"},
                    "arguments": {
                        "type": "object",
                        "properties": {},
                        "required": [],
                        "additionalProperties": False,
                    },
                },
                "required": ["name", "arguments"],
                "additionalProperties": False,
            },
        },
    },
    "required": ["action", "final_response", "tool_calls"],
    "additionalProperties": False,
}


def _build_arguments_schema(tools: list[dict[str, Any]]) -> dict[str, Any]:
    merged_properties: dict[str, Any] = {}
    for tool in tools:
        input_schema = tool.get("inputSchema")
        if not isinstance(input_schema, dict):
            continue
        properties = input_schema.get("properties")
        if not isinstance(properties, dict):
            continue
        for property_name, property_schema in properties.items():
            if property_name in merged_properties:
                continue
            if not isinstance(property_schema, dict):
                continue
            nullable_schema = dict(property_schema)
            property_type = nullable_schema.get("type")
            if isinstance(property_type, str):
                nullable_schema["type"] = [property_type, "null"]
            merged_properties[property_name] = nullable_schema

    return {
        "type": "object",
        "properties": merged_properties,
        "required": list(merged_properties.keys()),
        "additionalProperties": False,
    }


def get_llm_response_format(tools: list[dict[str, Any]]) -> dict[str, Any]:
    """
    Returns model_kwargs for structured output.
    For Anthropic — returns empty dict (handled via prompt, not response_format).
    For local/OpenAI — returns JSON schema response format.
    """
    provider = os.environ.get("LLM_PROVIDER", "local").strip().lower()

    if provider == "anthropic":
        return {}

    schema = deepcopy(LLM_DECISION_SCHEMA)
    tool_names = [str(tool.get("name")) for tool in tools if tool.get("name")]
    tool_call_schema = schema["properties"]["tool_calls"]["items"]
    tool_call_schema["properties"]["name"]["enum"] = tool_names
    tool_call_schema["properties"]["arguments"] = _build_arguments_schema(tools)

    return {
        "response_format": {
            "type": "json_schema",
            "json_schema": {
                "name": "agent_decision",
                "strict": True,
                "schema": schema,
            },
        }
    }


# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
# LLM response parsing helpers
# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------

def _strip_markdown_code_fence(content: str) -> str:
    stripped = content.strip()
    if not stripped.startswith("```"):
        return stripped
    lines = stripped.splitlines()
    if len(lines) < 3:
        return stripped
    if not lines[-1].strip().startswith("```"):
        return stripped
    return "\n".join(lines[1:-1]).strip()


def _parse_llm_json(content: str) -> dict[str, Any]:
    content_stripped = content.strip()

    # Handle Claude's <function_calls> XML format
    if "<function_calls>" in content_stripped:
        match = re.search(r'<function_calls>(.*?)</function_calls>', content_stripped, re.DOTALL)
        if match:
            calls_text = match.group(1).strip()
            try:
                calls = json.loads(calls_text)
                if isinstance(calls, list):
                    return {
                        "action": "tool",
                        "final_response": "",
                        "tool_calls": [
                            {
                                "name": c["name"],
                                "arguments": c.get("arguments", c.get("parameters", {}))
                            }
                            for c in calls
                        ]
                    }
            except json.JSONDecodeError:
                pass

    # Extract JSON from ```json ... ``` fence anywhere in content
    fence_match = re.search(r'```(?:json)?\s*(\{.*?\})\s*```', content_stripped, re.DOTALL)
    if fence_match:
        try:
            parsed = json.loads(fence_match.group(1))
            if isinstance(parsed, dict):
                return parsed
        except json.JSONDecodeError:
            pass

    # Find raw JSON object anywhere in content
    json_match = re.search(r'\{.*\}', content_stripped, re.DOTALL)
    if json_match:
        try:
            parsed = json.loads(json_match.group(0))
            if isinstance(parsed, dict):
                return parsed
        except json.JSONDecodeError:
            pass

    # Try direct parse — pure JSON response with no surrounding text
    try:
        parsed = json.loads(_strip_markdown_code_fence(content_stripped))
        if not isinstance(parsed, dict):
            raise RuntimeError("LLM JSON response must be an object")
        return parsed
    except json.JSONDecodeError:
        pass

    raise RuntimeError(
        "Could not extract JSON from LLM response: {}".format(content_stripped[:200])
    )


def _normalize_llm_decision(parsed: dict[str, Any]) -> dict[str, Any]:
    action = parsed.get("action")

    if action == "final":
        return {"action": "final", "final_response": parsed["final_response"]}

    if action == "tool":
        tool_calls = parsed.get("tool_calls")
        if not isinstance(tool_calls, list) or not tool_calls:
            raise RuntimeError("LLM tool decision must include a non-empty 'tool_calls' array")
        return {
            "action": "tool",
            "tool_calls": [{"name": t["name"], "arguments": t["arguments"]} for t in tool_calls],
        }

    if "final_response" in parsed:
        return {"action": "final", "final_response": parsed["final_response"]}

    tool_call = parsed.get("tool_call")
    if isinstance(tool_call, dict):
        return {
            "action": "tool",
            "tool_calls": [{"name": tool_call["name"], "arguments": tool_call["arguments"]}],
        }

    tool_calls = parsed.get("tool_calls")
    if isinstance(tool_calls, list) and tool_calls:
        return {
            "action": "tool",
            "tool_calls": [{"name": t["name"], "arguments": t["arguments"]} for t in tool_calls],
        }

    raise RuntimeError("LLM response must include either 'final_response' or 'tool_call'")


# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Anthropic-specific call — bypasses LangChain entirely
# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------

def _call_anthropic(
    client_dict: dict,
    system_prompt: str,
    messages: list[dict[str, str]],
    tool_catalog: str,
) -> dict[str, Any]:
    client  = client_dict["_client"]
    model   = client_dict["_model"]
    timeout = client_dict["_timeout"]

    formatted_prompt = system_prompt.format(tool_catalog=tool_catalog)

    # Anthropic only accepts "user" and "assistant" roles
    anthropic_messages = []
    for msg in messages:
        role    = msg.get("role", "user")
        content = msg.get("content", "")
        if role == "system":
            continue
        anthropic_messages.append({"role": role, "content": content})

    response = client.messages.create(
        model=model,
        max_tokens=4096,
        system=formatted_prompt,
        messages=anthropic_messages,
        timeout=timeout,
    )

    content = response.content[0].text
    print("\n[anthropic] Raw response preview:")
    print(content[:400])

    return _normalize_llm_decision(_parse_llm_json(content))


# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Public convenience function used by reason nodes
# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------

def call_llm(
    llm: Any,
    system_prompt: str,
    messages: list[dict[str, str]],
    tool_catalog: str,
) -> dict[str, Any]:
    """Invoke the LLM and return a parsed decision dict.
    Handles both Anthropic and local/OpenAI providers.
    """
    # Anthropic path — use SDK directly
    if isinstance(llm, dict) and llm.get("_type") == "anthropic":
        return _call_anthropic(llm, system_prompt, messages, tool_catalog)

    # Local / OpenAI / Cloudflare path — use LangChain
    formatted_prompt = system_prompt.format(tool_catalog=tool_catalog)
    llm_messages = [{"role": "system", "content": formatted_prompt}] + messages

    result = llm.invoke(llm_messages)
    content = result.content
    if not isinstance(content, str):
        raise RuntimeError("LLM response content must be a string")

    try:
        return _normalize_llm_decision(_parse_llm_json(content))
    except Exception:
        print("\n[llm] Raw LLM response before crash:")
        print(content)
        raise


# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Tool output persistence helper used by tool nodes
# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------

def write_tool_result(tool_output: str, path: Path) -> None:
    """Write the MCP tool output to a file, pretty-printing JSON if possible."""
    stripped = tool_output.strip()
    try:
        parsed = json.loads(stripped)
    except json.JSONDecodeError:
        text = tool_output if tool_output.endswith("\n") else tool_output + "\n"
    else:
        text = json.dumps(parsed, indent=2, ensure_ascii=False) + "\n"
    path.parent.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
    path.write_text(text, encoding="utf-8")
```

```python
from __future__ import annotations
from typing import Any
from _runtime.llm import call_llm


# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
# System prompt — edit this to change how the agent thinks and behaves.
# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------

SYSTEM_PROMPT = """You are a spatial accessibility assistant for floor plans. You use tools to analyze and modify layouts.

PROFILES: wheelchair, autistic, elderly, visually_impaired, hearing_impaired.
Default to wheelchair if unspecified.

TOOLS:
- check_door_widths(min_door_width): returns conflict door IDs
- widen_doors(door_ids, target_width): MODIFIES doors to a new width
- shortest_path, get_visibility, collision_detector_sphere: full analysis

DOOR FIX WORKFLOW — MANDATORY EVERY STEP:

When the user asks to FIX, WIDEN, REPAIR, or MODIFY doors:

STEP 1: Call check_door_widths with min_door_width=0.9 (wheelchair) or appropriate profile width.

STEP 2: Look at the "conflicts" array in the result.

STEP 3: You MUST call widen_doors NEXT. Do not skip this step. Do not assume widen_doors was already called. Do not respond with "final" until widen_doors has returned a result.

Format for STEP 3 call:
{{"action":"tool","final_response":"","tool_calls":[{{"name":"widen_doors","arguments":{{"door_ids":"d03,d04,d09,d10","target_width":0.9}}}}]}}

The door_ids string MUST be a comma-separated list of the conflict IDs from STEP 2. Example: if conflicts is ["d03","d04","d09","d10"], door_ids must be "d03,d04,d09,d10".

STEP 4: Only AFTER widen_doors returns a result with "modified" array, respond with action "final" summarizing what was actually modified.

CRITICAL RULES:
- NEVER claim doors were widened unless widen_doors has been called and returned successfully.
- NEVER skip widen_doors when the user asks to fix doors.
- NEVER call the same tool twice in a row.
- If widen_doors returns "modified": [], that means nothing was changed — report this honestly.

For general accessibility analysis (no door fix request): call shortest_path, get_visibility, collision_detector_sphere once each, then respond final.

OUTPUT (strict JSON, no markdown):
{{"action":"final"|"tool","final_response":"...","tool_calls":[{{"name":"<name>","arguments":{{...}}}}]}}

If action is "final": tool_calls is [], answer in final_response.
If action is "tool": final_response is "", call in tool_calls.

Tools available: {tool_catalog}
"""


# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Reason node — the LLM decision step in the graph.
# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------

def build_reason_node(llm):
    """Return a reason node function ready to be added to a LangGraph StateGraph."""

    def reason_node(state):
        print("\nReasoning with LLM...")
        result = call_llm(llm, SYSTEM_PROMPT, state["messages"], state["tool_catalog"])

        # If the LLM decided no more actions are needed (action is final), set the final response in the state and clear pending tool calls
        if result["action"] == "final":
            state["final_response"] = result["final_response"]
            state["pending_tool_calls"] = None

        # If the LLM decided the action is to use a tool, set the pending tool calls
        else:
            state["pending_tool_calls"] = result["tool_calls"]

        return state

    return reason_node

```

from __future__ import annotations
from typing import Any
from _runtime.llm import call_llm


# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
# System prompt — edit this to change how the agent thinks and behaves.
# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------

SYSTEM_PROMPT = """You are an assistant that helps users work with a building layout.

The MCP tools listed below are a toolbox: you may call them when they help achieve the user's goal. Choose tools and arguments only based on the user's request, the tool descriptions, and each tool's inputSchema. Do not assume any particular tool is required for a given instruction.

Always ground your reasoning in the current layout JSON shown in the user message. That payload is loaded from the repository's layout_input/layout_schema.json and defines the structure, attribute names, ids, and nested objects you should use for context (for example which keys exist, how entities reference each other, and what values are valid to mention or pass through).

If the user's goal cannot be satisfied without information that is missing from their message or from that layout JSON, respond with action "final" and ask a concise clarifying question.

After a tool result appears in the conversation, decide whether another tool call is needed or whether to respond with action "final" (for example to confirm completion or summarize what happened, including any output path or details echoed from the tool result when relevant).

Toolbox (name, description, and inputSchema for each tool):
{tool_catalog}

Return strictly valid JSON with exactly this shape:
{{
  "action": "final" | "tool",
  "final_response": "...",
  "tool_calls": [{{"name": "<tool-name>", "arguments": {{...}}}}, ...]
}}

Output rules:
- Return JSON only, with no prose or explanation.
- Do not use markdown code fences.
- If action is "final", set tool_calls to [] and put the answer in final_response.
- If action is "tool", set final_response to "" and put one or more tool calls in tool_calls.
"""


# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Reason node — the LLM decision step in the graph.
# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------

def build_reason_node(llm):
    """Return a reason node function ready to be added to a LangGraph StateGraph."""

    def reason_node(state):
        print("\nReasoning with LLM...")
        result = call_llm(llm, SYSTEM_PROMPT, state["messages"], state["tool_catalog"])

        # If the LLM decided no more actions are needed (action is final), set the final response in the state and clear pending tool calls
        if result["action"] == "final":
            state["final_response"] = result["final_response"]
            state["pending_tool_calls"] = None

        # If the LLM decided the action is to use a tool, set the pending tool calls
        else:
            state["pending_tool_calls"] = result["tool_calls"]

        return state

    return reason_node

```python
def call_llm_simple(
    llm: Any,
    system_prompt: str,
    user_message: str,
) -> dict[str, Any] | None:
    """
    Simplified LLM call for pre-agent nodes.
    No tool_catalog needed — returns parsed JSON or None.
    Use this for profile_agent and space_type_agent.
    Unlike call_llm(), no action/tool_calls schema expected.
    """
    try:
        # Anthropic path — use SDK directly
        if isinstance(llm, dict) and llm.get("_type") == "anthropic":
            result = _call_anthropic(llm, system_prompt,
                [{"role": "user", "content": user_message}], "")
            return result if isinstance(result, dict) else None

        # Local/OpenAI path — use LangChain
        messages = [
            {"role": "system", "content": system_prompt},
            {"role": "user", "content": user_message},
        ]
        result = llm.invoke(messages)
        content = result.content
        if not isinstance(content, str):
            return None
        cleaned = _strip_markdown_code_fence(content)
        parsed = json.loads(cleaned)
        return parsed if isinstance(parsed, dict) else None

    except Exception as exc:
        print(f"[llm_simple] Failed: {exc}")
        return None
```

def call_llm_simple(
    llm: Any,
    system_prompt: str,
    user_message: str,
) -> dict[str, Any] | None:
    """
    Simplified LLM call for pre-agent nodes 
    (profile_agent, space_type_agent).
    No tool_catalog needed — returns parsed

    Unlike call_llm(), no action/tool_calls

        return parsed if isinstance(parsed, dict) else None
